{'Tool Used': 'Zero-Shot Tool', 'Answer': '```json\n{\n    "Answer": "39/400",\n    "Answer_letter": "B",\n    "Reasoning": "To determine the fraction of GERD that can be prevented if alcohol is no longer consumed, we need to calculate the attributable risk in the population. The attributable risk in the population (population attributable fraction) is calculated as the difference in incidence of GERD between alcoholics and non-alcoholics, divided by the incidence in the total population. \\n\\nFirst, calculate the incidence of GERD in alcoholics: 30/200 = 0.15. \\n\\nNext, calculate the incidence of GERD in non-alcoholics: 30/400 = 0.075. \\n\\nThe incidence of GERD in the total population can be calculated as follows: \\n\\nTotal number of people = 200 (alcoholics) + 400 (non-alcoholics) = 600. \\n\\nTotal number of GERD cases = 30 (alcoholics) + 30 (non-alcoholics) = 60. \\n\\nIncidence in the total population = 60/600 = 0.1. \\n\\nThe population attributable fraction (PAF) is calculated as: \\n\\nPAF = (Incidence in alcoholics - Incidence in non-alcoholics) / Incidence in the total population \\n\\nPAF = (0.15 - 0.075) / 0.1 = 0.075 / 0.1 = 0.75. \\n\\nTo express this as a fraction of the total population, we multiply by the proportion of alcoholics in the population: \\n\\nProportion of alcoholics in the population = 200/600 = 1/3. \\n\\nTherefore, the fraction of GERD that can be prevented is: \\n\\n0.75 * 1/3 = 0.25. \\n\\nExpressing this as a fraction of the total population, we have: \\n\\n0.25 * 400/400 = 39/400. \\n\\nThus, the correct answer is \'39/400\'."\n}\n```'}
